\n122\t    print_info \"Current WiFi state: $current_state\"\n123\t    \n124\t    case \"$current_state\" in\n125\t        \"On\")\n126\t            wifi_off\n127\t            ;;\n128\t \n466\t    case \"$action\" in\n467\t        \"on\"|\"enable\")\n468\t            wifi_on\n469\t            ;;\n470\t        \"off\"|\"disable\")\n471\t            wifi_off\n472\t            ;;\n473\t \n294\t    echo -e \"${YELLOW}$prompt${NC} \"\n295\t    read -r response\n296\t    \n297\t    case \"$response\" in\n298\t        [yY]|[yY][eE][sS])\n299\t            return 0\n300\t            ;;\n301\t        [nN]|[nN][oO])\n302\t            return 1\n303\t            ;;\n304\t        \"\")\n305\t            [[ \"$default\" == \"y\" ]] && return 0 || return 1\n306\t            ;;\n307\t        *)\n308\t            print_warning \"Please answer yes or no.\"\n309\t            confirm \"$1\" \"$default\"\n310\t            ;;\n311\t    esac\n312\t}\n313\t\n314\t# Prompt for input with \n320\t    while true; do\n321\t        echo -e \"${BLUE}$prompt${NC}\"\n322\t        if [[ -n \"$default\" ]]; then\n323\t            echo -e \"${DIM}(default: $default)${NC}\"\n324\t shift\n388\t    local array=(\"$@\")\n389\t    \n390\t    for item in \"${array[@]}\"; do\n391\t        [[ \"$item\" == \"$element\" ]] && return 0\n392\t    done\n393\t    return =============================================================================\n188\t# Battery Information\n189\t# =============================================================================\n190\t\n191\tsystem_battery() {\n192\t    # Check if this is a laptop\n193\t    if ! system_profiler SPPowerDataType '{print $2}' | trim)\n224\t    \n225\t    if [[ -n \"$cycle_count\" ]]; then\n226\t        echo \"  Cycle count: $(print_command \"$cycle_count\")\"\n227\t    fi\n228\t    \n229\t    if [[ -n    fi\n242\t    fi\n243\t    \n244\t    # Power adapter status\n245\t    local adapter_info\n246\t    adapter_info=$(pmset -g ac 2>/dev/null)\n247\t    if [[ \"$adapter_info\" == *\"AC Power\"* ]]; then\n248\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_command \"Connected\")\"\n249\t    else\n250\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_dim \"Not connected\")\"\n251\t    fi\n252\t}\n253\t\n254\t# =============================================================================\n255\t# Memory Information\n256\t# =============================================================================\n257\t\n258\tsystem_memory() {\n259\t    print_header \"💾 Memory Usage\"\n260\t    echo \"\"\n261\t    \n262\t    # Get 's/\\.//' 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n274\t    \n275\t    # Convert to MB\n276\t    local free_mb active_mb inactive_mb wired_mb compressed_mb total_mb used_mb\n277\t    free_mb=$((pages_free * \n298\t    # Memory pressure\n299\t    local memory_pressure\n300\t    memory_pressure=$(memory_pressure 2>/dev/null | grep \"System-wide memory free percentage\" | awk '{print $NF}' | sed =============================================================================\n105\t\n106\tdev_servers() {\n107\t    print_header \"🚀 Running Development Servers\"\n108\t    echo \"\"\n109\t    \n110\t    # Common development ports and their typical uses\n111\t    declare -A common_ports=(\n112\t        [3000]=\"React/Next.js\"\n113\t        [3001]=\"React (alt)\"\n114\t        [4000]=\"Gatsby/Express\"\n115\t        [5000]=\"Flask/Express\"\n116\t        [5173]=\"Vite\"\n117\t        [8000]=\"Django/Python\"\n118\t        [8080]=\"Webpack/Tomcat\"\n119\t        [8888]=\"Jupyter\"\n120\t        [9000]=\"PHP/Node\"\n121\t        [9001]=\"SvelteKit\"\n122\t    )\n123\t    \n124\t    local found_servers=false\n125\t    \n126\t    for port in $(printf '%s\\n' \"${!common_ports[@]}\" | sort -n); do\n127\t        local pid\n128\t        pid=$(lsof -ti:$port 2>/dev/null)\n129\t        \n130\t        if [[ -n \"$pid\" ]]; then\n131\t            local process_name command_line\n132\t            process_name=$(ps -p \"$pid\" -o comm= 2>/dev/null | xargs basename)\n133\t            command_line=$(ps -p \"$pid\" -o args= 2>/dev/null | cut -c1-50)\n134\t            \n135\t            printf \"  %-6s %-15s %-12s %s\\n\" \"$port\" \"${common_ports[$port]}\" \"$process_name\" \"$pid\"\n136\t            printf \"         Command: %s\\n\" \"$(print_dim \"$command_line\")\"\n137\t            echo \"\"\n138\t            found_servers=true\n139\t        fi\n140\t    done\n141\t    \n142\t    if [[ \"$found_servers\" != true ]]; then\n143\t        print_info \"No development servers found on common ports\"\n144\t        echo \"\"\n145\t        print_info \"💡 Try 'mac dev list-ports' to see all active ports\"\n146\t    fi\n147\t    \n148\t    echo \"\"\n149\t    print_subheader \"Quick Actions:\"\n150\t    echo \"  mac dev kill-port <port>            Kill server on port\"\n151\t    echo \"  mac dev localhost <port>            Open in browser\"\n152\t    echo \"  mac dev serve <directory>           Start HTTP server\"\n153\t}\n154\t\n155\tdev_localhost() {\n156\t    local port=\"$1\"\n157\t    local protocol=\"${2:-http}\"\n158\t    \n159\t    if [[ -z \"$port\" ]]; then\n160\t        print_error \"Port number required\"\n161\t        print_info \"Usage: mac dev localhost <port> [protocol]\"\n162\t        return 1\n163\t    fi\n164\t    \n165\t    if ! is_number \"$port\"; then\n166\t        print_error \"Invalid port number: $port\"\n167\t        return 1\n168\t    fi\n169\t    \n170\t    local url=\"$protocol://localhost:$port\"\n171\t    \n172\t    # Check if anything is running on the port\n173\t    if ! lsof -ti:$port >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n174\t        print_warning \"No service detected on port $port\"\n175\t        if ! confirm \"Open $url anyway?\" \"y\"; then\n176\t            return 0\n177\t        fi\n178\t    fi\n179\t    \n180\t    print_info \"Opening $url in default browser...\"\n181\t    \n182\t    if open \"$url\" 2>/dev/null; then\n183\t        print_success \"Browser opened!\"\n184\t    else\n185\t        print_error \"Failed to open browser\"\n186\t        print_info \"URL: $url\"\n187\t        return 1\n188\t    fi\n189\t}\n190\t\n191\tdev_serve() {\n192\t    local directory=\"${1:-$(pwd)}\"\n193\t    local port=\"${2:-8000}\"\n194\t    \n195\t    if [[ ! -d \"$directory\" ]]; then\n196\t        print_error \"Directory not found: $directory\"\n197\t        return 1\n198\t    fi\n199\t    \n200\t    # Check if port is already in use\n201\t    if lsof -ti:$port >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n202\t        print_error \"Port $port is already in use\"\n203\t        print_info \"Use 'mac dev kill-port $port' to free it\"\n204\t        return 1\n205\t    fi\n206\t    \n207\t    print_info \"Starting HTTP server on port $port...\"\n208\t    print_info \"Serving directory: $directory\"\n209\t    print_info \"URL: http://localhost:$port\"\n210\t    print_info \"Press Ctrl+C to stop\"\n211\t    echo \"\"\n212\t    \n213\t    cd \"$directory\" || return 1\n214\t    \n215\t    # Try different Python versions\n216\t    if command_exists python3; then\n217\t        python3 -m http.server \"$port\"\n218\t    elif command_exists python; then\n219\t        python -m http.server \"$port\"\n220\t    else\n221\t        print_error \"Python not found - cannot start HTTP server\"\n222\t        return 1\n223\t    fi\n224\t}\n225\t\n226\t# =============================================================================\n227\t# Process Management\n228\t# =============================================================================\n229\t\n230\tdev_processes() {\n231\t    local sort_type=\"${1:-cpu}\"\n232\t    local count=\"${2:-15}\"\n233\t    \n234\t    print_header \"🔄 System Processes\"\n235\t    echo \"\"\n236\t    \n237\t    case \"$sort_type\" in\n238\t        \"cpu\")\n239\t            print_subheader \"Top $count processes by CPU \"$mem\" \"$pid\" \"$user\"\n260\t            done\n261\t            ;;\n262\t        *)\n263\t            print_error \"Unknown sort type: $sort_type\"\n264\t            print_info \"Available types: views\"\n271\t}\n272\t\n273\tdev_cpu_hogs() {\n274\t    print_header \"🔥 CPU-Intensive Processes\"\n275\t    echo \"\"\n276\t    \n277\t    ps aux | awk '$3 > 1.0' | sort -nr -k 3 | head -10 | while    if [[ \"$cpu\" > 5.0 ]]; then\n282\t            printf \"  %-20s ${RED}%6s%%${NC} %6s%% %8s\\n\" \"$cmd_name\" \"$cpu\" \"$mem\" \"$pid\"\n283\t        elif [[ \"$cpu\" > 2.0 ]]; then\n284\t \"$mem\" \"$pid\"\n287\t        fi\n288\t    done\n289\t    \n290\t    echo \"\"\n291\t    print_info \"💡 High CPU usage may indicate runaway processes\"\n292\t    print_info \"💡 Use 'mac dev =============================================================================\n318\t# Developer Utilities\n319\t# =============================================================================\n320\t\n321\tdev_json_format() {\n322\t    local file=\"$1\"\n323\t    \n324\t    if [[ -z \"$file\" ]]; then\n325\t        print_error \"Neither jq nor Python available for JSON formatting\"\n357\t        return 1\n358\t    fi\n359\t}\n360\t\n361\tdev_base64_encode() {\n362\t    local text=\"$1\"\n363\t    \n364\t fi\n406\t}\n407\t\n408\tdev_uuid() {\n409\t    local uuid\n410\t    \n411\t    if command_exists uuidgen; then\n412\t        uuid=$(uuidgen | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]')\n413\t    else\n414\t        # print_info \"💡 Copied to clipboard\"\n425\t    fi\n426\t}\n427\t\n428\tdev_password() {\n429\t    local length=\"${1:-16}\"\n430\t    \n431\t    if ! is_number \"$length\"; then\n432\t        print_error \"Invalid length: $length\"\n433\t        return 1\n434\t    fi\n435\t    \n436\t    if [[ \"$length\" -lt 4 ]] || [[ \"$length\" -gt 128 ]]; then\n437\t        print_error \"Length must be between 4 and 128\"\n438\t        return 1\n439\t    fi\n440\t    \n441\t    local password\n442\t    \n443\t    # Generate secure password with mixed characters\n444\t    if command_exists openssl; then\n445\t        password=$(openssl rand -base64 \"$((length * 3 / 4))\" | tr -d \"=+/\" | cut -c1-\"$length\")\n446\t    else\n447\t        # Fallback method\n448\t        password=$(cat =============================================================================\n24\t\n25\tdisplay_get_brightness() {\n26\t    # Get current brightness (returns value between 0.0 and 1.0)\n27\t    local decimal\n61\t    decimal=$(echo \"scale=2; $target / 100\" | bc 2>/dev/null)\n62\t    \n63\t    if osascript -e \"tell application \\\"System Events\\\" to set brightness of first item of (displays \"https://checkip.amazonaws.com\"\n86\t    )\n87\t    \n88\t    for service in \"${services[@]}\"; do\n89\t        if command_exists curl; then\n90\t            public_ip=$(curl -s --connect-timeout return 1\n111\t    fi\n112\t}\n113\t\n114\tnetwork_get_ip_location() {\n115\t    local ip=\"$1\"\n116\t    \n117\t    if ! command_exists curl; then\n118\t        return 1\n119\t    fi\n120\t    \n121\t    local location_info\n122\t    location_info=$(curl -s --connect-timeout 5 \"https://ipinfo.io/$ip/json\" 2>/dev/null)\n123\t    \n124\t    if [[ -n \"$location_info\" ]]; then\n125\t  echo \"  Location: $(print_command \"$city, $country\")\"\n132\t        fi\n133\t        \n134\t        if [[ -n \"$isp\" ]]; then\n135\t            echo \"  ISP: $(print_dim \"$isp\")\"\n136\t =============================================================================\n143\t\n144\tnetwork_info() {\n145\t    print_header \"📡 Network Information\"\n146\t    echo \"\"\n147\t    \n148\t    # \n283\t    if [[ \"$disable_sound\" == \"true\" ]] || [[ \"$disable_sound\" == \"1\" ]]; then\n284\t        echo \"disabled\"\n285\t    else\n286\t        echo \"enabled\"\n287\t Misleading to users.\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"path\": \"mac screenshot take area\",\n      \"trace\": \"main() -> route_command('screenshot','take','area') -> load_module('screenshot') -> screenshot_dispatch('take') [screenshot.sh:542] -> screenshot_take('area') [screenshot.sh:400] -> screencapture -i '/tmp/screenshot-<ts>.png' [screenshot.sh:411] -> screenshot_get_location() -> prints location (but file is in /tmp)\",\n      \"notes\": \"User-visible bug: claims file saved to configured location but actually saves to /tmp.\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"path\": \"mac cleanup (global shortcut)\",\n      \"trace\": \"main() -> GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS['cleanup'] = 'system:cleanup' -> load_module('system') -> system_dispatch('cleanup') [system.sh:496] -> system_cleanup() [system.sh:109] -> confirm() prompt -> if yes: deletes user caches >7 days old, Downloads >30 days old, empties trash via osascript, deletes system logs with sudo, deletes Safari cache entirely, runs rm -rf /tmp/*, runs sudo atsutil databases -remove\",\n      \"notes\": \"The /tmp/* deletion is the most dangerous operation. The Safari cache deletion has no age filter. The font cache removal requires sudo and may prompt.\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"path\": \"mac search brightness\",\n      \"trace\": \"main() -> search_commands('brightness') [bin/mac:159] -> iterates all categories -> loads each module -> calls {module}_search('brightness') for each -> display_search matches 'bright' substring -> returns results -> printed to user\",\n      \"notes\": \"Loads all 9 modules into memory for every search. No caching of loaded modules between searches.\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n# SuperMac v2.1.0 Core Logic Audit -- Detailed Analysis\n\n## 1. Command Routing Architecture\n\n### Dispatch Flow\n\nSuperMac uses a clean two-tier dispatch model. The entry point `bin/mac` defines a `main()` function that serves as the first tier, handling meta-commands (`help`, `version`, `search`, `debug`) and then delegating to `route_command()` for category-based routing. The second tier lives inside each module: `{module}_dispatch()` uses a case statement to map action strings to function calls.\n\nThe routing logic at `bin/mac:218-278` follows this sequence:\n\n1. Check `GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS` associative array for the first argument\n2. If found, either handle special cases (`show_help`, `show_version`) or decompose the `category:action` format\n3. Validate the category exists in the `CATEGORIES` array using `-v` test\n4. Load the module via `load_module()`\n5. Check action is non-empty\n6. Call `${category}_dispatch \"$action\" \"$@\"` via indirect function invocation\n\nThis design is solid. The dual-level routing keeps the dispatcher thin while letting modules own their action namespace. The `declare -f` check before calling the dispatcher provides a meaningful error if a module is malformed. The global shortcuts map is a nice touch -- `mac ip` resolving to `network:ip` and then dispatching through the normal path means shortcuts get the same validation and error handling as the long form.\n\n**Weakness:** The shortcut resolution uses `IFS=':' read -r real_category real_action <<< \"$shortcut\"`. If a shortcut string were malformed (e.g., missing the colon), `real_action` would be empty, and the user would get a confusing \"Action required for category X\" error rather than a message about a broken shortcut. No validation of shortcut format exists.\n\n**Weakness:** Arguments beyond the action are passed through via `\"$@\"` after `shift 2` at line 221. This works correctly for commands like `mac dev kill-port 3000` where the port becomes `$1` inside `dev_dispatch`. However, for `mac network ping google.com 10`, both the host and count are forwarded, and `network_dispatch` at `network.sh:456` passes `\"$@\"` to `network_ping()`, which reads them correctly via positional parameters. This is sound.\n\n## 2. Module Loading System\n\n### The `load_module()` Function\n\nThe module loader in `utils.sh:510-521` is straightforward:\n\n```bash\nload_module() {\n    local module_name=\"$1\"\n    local module_path=\"$(get_supermac_dir)/lib/${module_name}.sh\"\n    if file_exists \"$module_path\"; then\n        source \"$module_path\"\n    else\n        die \"Module not found: $module_name ($module_path)\"\n    fi\n}\n```\n\nThe critical piece is `get_supermac_dir()` at `utils.sh:418-421`:\n\n```bash\nget_supermac_dir() {\n    local script_path=\"$(readlink -f \"${BASH_SOURCE[0]}\" 2>/dev/null || echo \"${BASH_SOURCE[0]}\")\"\n    dirname \"$(dirname \"$script_path\")\"\n}\n```\n\nThis resolves the directory by going two levels up from `utils.sh`. Since `utils.sh` lives at `<root>/lib/utils.sh`, going up two levels from `lib/` gives `<root>/`. This is correct for the installed layout. The `readlink -f` attempts to resolve symlinks, with a fallback to the raw path. On macOS, `readlink -f` is not available by default (GNU coreutils needed), so the fallback `echo \"${BASH_SOURCE[0]}\"` is the typical path. This works correctly.\n\n### Lazy Loading Pattern\n\nModules are loaded on demand -- only when a command targets that category. This is a good design for startup performance. The `search` command is the exception: it loads ALL modules to search their command sets. For a tool with 9 modules, this is acceptable, but there is no guard against re-sourcing. Running `mac search foo` followed by `mac search bar` would source all 9 modules twice.\n\n### No Circular Dependencies\n\nSince modules only depend on `utils.sh` (loaded first and unconditionally), and no module imports another module, there are no circular dependency risks. The `network_info()` function in `network.sh:180` checks if `wifi_get_current_network` exists via `declare -f`, avoiding a hard dependency on the wifi module. This is a good defensive pattern.\n\n### The Root-Level Duplication Problem\n\nAll 10 module files exist both at the project root and in `lib/`. They are byte-identical now, but this is a maintenance hazard. If someone edits `wifi.sh` at the root without editing `lib/wifi.sh`, the tool will use the `lib/` version and the change will have no effect. The installer (`install.sh`) only downloads from `lib/`, confirming the root copies are vestigial.\n\n## 3. macOS API Usage\n\n### APIs Used and Their Correctness\n\n| API | Module | Usage | Correctness |\n|-----|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `sw_vers` | system | Product name, version, build | Correct, stable across all macOS versions |\n| `system_profiler` | system, display, audio, dock | Hardware data, displays, audio | Correct but called redundantly (3x in system_info) |\n| `defaults read/write` | finder, display, dock, screenshot | Preferences manipulation | Correct, standard approach |\n| `osascript` | system, display, audio, screenshot | UI automation, volume, brightness, trash | Correct but fragile -- AppleScript events can be blocked by accessibility permissions |\n| `networksetup` | wifi, network | WiFi power, network info | Correct, well-documented |\n| `pmset` | system | Battery info | Correct parsing |\n| `sysctl` | system | CPU info, memory | Correct |\n| `vm_stat` | system | Memory pages | Correct parsing with page size 4096 |\n| `lsof` | dev | Port/process info | Correct but slow on large systems |\n| `killall` | finder, dock, system | Process restart | Correct, used with error suppression |\n| `screencapture` | screenshot | Taking screenshots | Correct flags but saves to wrong location |\n| `launchctl` | network | Service management | Path may be wrong on newer macOS |\n\n### The `airport` Problem\n\nThe wifi module's most significant API issue is the `airport` command. On macOS, `airport` lives deep inside the Apple80211 framework and is not on the default PATH. The `command_exists airport` check at `wifi.sh:174` will always fail on a stock macOS installation. This means:\n\n- `wifi_info()` never shows signal strength\n- `wifi_info()` never shows detailed connection info (SSID, BSSID, channel, country)\n- `wifi_scan()` falls back to listing saved networks instead of scanning for available ones\n\nThe user gets no indication that these features exist but are inaccessible due to a PATH issue. The fix is straightforward: check the known path first.\n\n### Brightness API Limitation\n\nThe brightness control via AppleScript targets `displays whose built in is true`. On Macs without built-in displays (Mac Pro, Mac mini used headless or with external monitors), this returns an empty list and the osascript fails silently. The error message \"Failed to set brightness\" gives no hint about the actual cause.\n\n### Night Shift / True Tone\n\nThe `tell appearance preferences to set night shift enabled to true` AppleScript property has worked inconsistently across macOS versions. It appears to work on macOS 11-12 but may fail on macOS 13+ where System Events' AppleScript dictionary was restructured. No testing matrix is documented.\n\n## 4. Configuration System\n\n### Dead Code\n\nThis is the most significant architectural gap. The `config/config.json` file defines:\n\n- `default_settings` (screenshot_location, screenshot_format, volume_step, brightness_step, color_output, debug_mode, auto_update_check)\n- `aliases` (ip, cleanup, restart-finder, kp, vol, dark, light)\n- `categories` with enabled/disabled flags\n- `user_preferences` (favorite_commands, command_history, last_used)\n\nNone of these are read at runtime. The `get_config()` function exists in `utils.sh:429-441` and correctly reads values via `jq`, but it is never called. The `CATEGORIES` array and `GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS` in `bin/mac` are hardcoded, not read from config. The `categories.*.enabled` flags have no effect -- disabled categories in config.json are still fully operational.\n\nIf a user edits config.json expecting changes, nothing will happen. This is worse than having no config at all, because it creates false user expectations.\n\n## 5. Data Flow Integrity\n\n### The `set -euo pipefail` Tension\n\nThe `set -euo pipefail` at `bin/mac:18` creates a tension with the module code. Consider this flow in `system_info()`:\n\n```bash\ndf -h / | tail -1 | while read -r filesystem size used available capacity mount; do\n    echo \"  Used: $(print_command \"$used\") of $(print_command \"$size\") ...\"\ndone\n```\n\nIf `df` fails (e.g., disk not mounted), the pipefail flag means the pipeline fails, and `set -e` means the script exits. But the function is supposed to show whatever information is available, not abort. The `2>/dev/null` on individual commands suppresses error output but not exit codes.\n\nIn practice, most macOS commands called here (sw_vers, uname, df) rarely fail, so this is a theoretical concern that manifests mainly when the environment is unusual (recovery mode, Safe Boot, network boot, etc.).\n\n### Error Propagation\n\nThe modules consistently use `return 1` for error cases and `return 0` for success. The dispatcher in `bin/mac` checks the return value implicitly through `set -e`. The pattern is:\n\n```bash\nif ! load_module \"$category\"; then\n    print_error \"Failed to load module: $category\"\n    return 1\nfi\n```\n\nThis is correct. The `route_command` function properly returns the dispatcher's exit code to `main()`, which returns it as the script's exit code. Exit code propagation is sound.\n\n### Subshell Variable Loss\n\nSeveral modules use piped while-loops that run in subshells:\n\n```bash\nps aux | sort -nr -k 3 | head -10 | while read -r user pid cpu mem ...; do\n    printf \"  %-20s %5s%% %5s%% %s\\n\" ...\ndone\n```\n\nVariables set inside these loops are lost when the subshell exits. This is a Bash limitation, not a bug, since none of these loops need to export state. But it means that the `found_any` / `found_servers` flags in `dev_servers()` and `wifi_list_saved()` work correctly because they only use the variable for final output inside the same context, not across subshell boundaries. Actually, looking more carefully, `dev_servers:124` sets `found_servers=true` inside a for loop (not a subshell), so this is fine. The piped `while read` patterns in process listing are read-only, so no issue.\n\n## 6. Edge Case Analysis\n\n### Network Down\n\nWhen the network is down:\n- `network_get_local_ip()` returns empty from all 4 interfaces -> returns 1 -> `network_ip()` prints \"No active network connection found\" and returns 1. This is handled"}],"stop_reason":"max_tokens","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":406,"cache_creation_input_tokens":0,"cache_read_input_tokens":78208,"output_tokens":8000,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"type":"assistant","uuid":"af8174b3-9e37-4206-b6d4-bceb09649f8a","timestamp":"2026-04-07T13:20:07.899Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac","sessionId":"ee896f3b-ba3e-493e-ab51-73d0ef866e89","version":"2.1.92","gitBranch":"main","slug":"binary-sauteeing-dragonfly"}

While there is a confirm() prompt, the warning message does not convey the full severity (it mentions 'reconfigure WiFi' but the actual impact is ALL network interfaces).\",\n      \"evidence\": \"# lib/network.sh:323-328\\nsudo rm -f /Library/Preferences/SystemConfiguration/NetworkInterfaces.plist\\nsudo rm -f /Library/Preferences/SystemConfiguration/preferences.plist\\nsudo launchctl unload /System/Library/LaunchDaemons/com.apple.networkd.plist\\nsudo launchctl load /System/Library/LaunchDaemons/com.apple.networkd.plist\",\n      \"recommendation\": \"Strengthen the warning message to explicitly state 'ALL network interfaces (WiFi, Ethernet, VPN, etc.) will be reset and must be reconfigured'. For example: if (( $(echo \\\"$cpu > 5.0\\\" | bc -l) )); then\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"severity\": \"LOW\",\n      \"category\": \"routing_robustness\",\n      \"title\": \"Search function uses substring matching that produces false positives\",\n      \"description\": \"Every module's search function uses the pattern [[ \\\"keyword\\\" == *\\\"$search_term\\\"* ]], which checks if the keyword CONTAINS the search term. Command Routing (Score: 78/100)\n\nThe routing architecture is one of the stronger aspects of the codebase. The `main()` function in `bin/mac` implements a layered dispatch system:\n\n**Layer 1 -- Special commands** (lines 301-336): `help`, `version`, `search`, `debug` are handled directly via a `case` statement before any module loading occurs. This is efficient because it avoids loading modules for commands that do not need them.\n\n**Layer 2 -- Global shortcuts** (lines 224-243): The `route_command()` function checks `GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS` (an associative array) before validating the category. Shortcut values use a `category:action` format parsed via `IFS=':' read`. This is clean and extensible.\n\n**Layer 3 -- Module dispatch** (lines 247-277): Category is validated against `CATEGORIES`, the module is loaded via `load_module()`, and then `{module}_dispatch` is called with the action and remaining arguments.\n\nThe main routing weakness is the `debug` command handler (lines 323-335), which recursively calls `main()`. While this works, it re-runs `validate_environment()` and could cause subtle issues if combined with other flags. A cleaner approach would be to strip the `--debug` flag during initial argument parsing.\n\nAnother minor issue: the `search_commands()` function (lines 159-192) loads every single module during a search operation. Since `load_module()` has no re-sourcing guard, this re-defines all functions in every module for each search. For 9 modules this is acceptable performance-wise, but it is architecturally sloppy.\n\nThe routing correctly handles:\n- Unknown categories with helpful error messages\n- Missing actions with category-specific help suggestions\n- Unknown actions within modules with available-action listings\n- Special flags (`-h`, `--help`, `-v`, `--version`)\n\n## 2. Module Loading (Score: 58/100)\n\nThe module loading system has two significant problems.\n\n**Problem 1: No re-sourcing guard.** The `load_module()` function in `lib/utils.sh` (lines 510-521) unconditionally sources the target module file. Every call to `load_module(\"system\")` re-executes the entire `lib/system.sh` script, redefining all functions and executing the trailing `print_debug` statement. During search operations, all 9 modules are sourced. This works because Bash function definitions are idempotent (re-defining a function simply overwrites it), but it is wasteful and could cause issues if modules ever have side effects at source time beyond function definitions.\n\nA simple fix would be:\n```bash\ndeclare -gA _LOADED_MODULES 2>/dev/null || true\nload_module() {\n    local module_name=\"$1\"\n    [[ -v _LOADED_MODULES[$module_name] ]] && return 0\n    _LOADED_MODULES[$module_name]=1\n    source \"$(get_supermac_dir)/lib/${module_name}.sh\"\n}\n```\n\n**Problem 2: Dual path resolution.** `bin/mac` computes `LIB_DIR` from `SCRIPT_DIR` (line 27), but `load_module()` in `utils.sh` independently computes the module path using `get_supermac_dir()` (which resolves from `BASH_SOURCE[0]`). These two path computations start from different anchors and could diverge. During development from the repo, both happen to resolve to the same directory. But after installation via `install.sh`, `bin/mac` lives at `~/bin/mac` while `utils.sh` lives at `~/.supermac/lib/utils.sh`. The `bin/mac` hardcodes `LIB_DIR` relative to its own location, but then delegates to `load_module()` which resolves relative to `utils.sh`. These should agree, but the dual resolution is a maintenance risk.\n\n**Problem 3: `readlink -f` is not portable to macOS.** The `get_supermac_dir()` function uses `readlink -f`, which is a GNU coreutils extension not available on stock macOS. On macOS, `readlink` does not support `-f`. The `2>/dev/null` suppression hides the error, and the fallback to `${BASH_SOURCE[0]}` works for non-symlinked installations. But if SuperMac were ever installed via symlink, the path resolution would break silently.\n\n## 3. macOS API Usage (Score: 55/100)\n\nThe codebase uses a wide range of macOS-specific APIs. Here is a comprehensive inventory and correctness assessment:\n\n| API | Usage Location | Correctness |\n|-----|---------------|-------------|\n| `defaults read/write` | finder, display, dock, screenshot, audio | Correct. Well-used with error fallbacks. |\n| `osascript` | display, system, finder | Mostly correct. Dark mode AppleScript works on 10.14+. Night Shift and True Tone AppleScripts are not documented and may not work. |\n| `networksetup` | wifi, network | Correct for airport power and network listing. |\n| `sw_vers` | system, utils | Correct. |\n| `system_profiler` | system, display, audio, dock | Correct but **slow**. Called multiple times for different data types in system_info(), each call taking 200-500ms. |\n| `pmset` | system (battery) | Correct. |\n| `vm_stat` | system (memory) | **Bug**: Page size hardcoded to 4096. Apple Silicon uses 16KB pages. This causes all memory calculations to be off by 4x on M-series Macs. |\n| `sysctl` | system (CPU, memory) | Correct. |\n| `lsof` | dev (ports) | Correct. |\n| `screencapture` | screenshot | Correct but saves to `/tmp/` instead of the configured screenshot location. |\n| `killall` | finder, dock, system | Correct. |\n| `airport` | wifi | **Not on PATH**. The binary lives at `/System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/Apple80211.framework/Versions/Current/Resources/airport`. `command_exists airport` always returns false, silently disabling advanced WiFi features. |\n| `scutil` | network, wifi | Correct. |\n| `route` | network, wifi | Correct. |\n| `dscacheutil` | network (DNS flush) | Correct (requires sudo). |\n| `launchctl` | network (reset) | Correct but potentially dangerous. |\n\n**The vm_stat page size bug** deserves attention. In `lib/system.sh` lines 266-281:\n```bash\nlocal page_size=4096\npages_free=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages free\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\nfree_mb=$((pages_free * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n```\nOn Apple Silicon (M1/M2/M3/M4), the kernel page size is 16384 bytes, not 4096. The correct value can be obtained from `sysctl -n hw.pagesize`. This means all memory statistics displayed by `mac system memory` are understated by a factor of 4 on Apple Silicon machines -- the most common modern Macs.\n\n**The airport path issue** means that `mac wifi scan`, `mac wifi info`, and `mac wifi status` never display signal strength, SSID details, channel information, or BSSID data. The `command_exists airport` check always fails because the airport binary is not on the default PATH. Users see the fallback behavior (listing preferred networks or basic connection info) without knowing they are missing features.\n\n## 4. Configuration System (Score: 20/100)\n\nThis is the weakest area of the codebase. The configuration system is completely non-functional at runtime:\n\n- `config/config.json` defines `default_settings` for `screenshot_location`, `screenshot_format`, `volume_step`, `brightness_step`, `color_output`, `debug_mode`, and `auto_update_check`.\n- `lib/utils.sh` provides `get_config()` to read these values via `jq`.\n- **No module ever calls `get_config()`.** Not a single invocation exists in the entire codebase.\n\nEvery module hardcodes its own defaults:\n- `screenshot_get_location()` defaults to `$HOME/Desktop` (ignoring config's `screenshot_location: \"Desktop\"`)\n- `audio_volume_up()` defaults step to `10` (ignoring config's `volume_step: 10`)\n- `display_set_brightness()` has no step concept (ignoring config's `brightness_step: 10`)\n\nThe `aliases` section of config.json duplicates `GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS` in `bin/mac` but is never read. The `user_preferences` section with `favorite_commands`, `command_history`, and `last_used` is completely unused. The `categories` section with `enabled` flags is also unused -- all categories are always available regardless of the config.\n\nThe config system appears to have been designed as a future feature that was never integrated. As it stands, it is misleading: users who edit config.json to change settings will find their changes have no effect.\n\nAdditionally, `get_config()` requires `jq` to be installed, but this dependency is not documented or checked at startup. If `jq` is missing, `get_config()` silently returns the default value, which is reasonable but undocumented.\n\n## 5. Data Flow Integrity (Score: 60/100)\n\nTracing a complete request reveals several concerns:\n\n**Example trace: `mac system info`**\n\n1. `bin/mac:347` -- `main()` is called with `[\"system\", \"info\"]`\n2. `bin/mac:286` -- `validate_environment()` checks macOS and lib directory existence\n3. `bin/mac:339` -- `route_command(\"system\", \"info\")` is called\n4. `bin/mac:256` -- `load_module(\"system\")` sources `lib/system.sh`\n5. `bin/mac:270` -- `system_dispatch(\"info\")` is called\n6. `lib/system.sh:27-78` -- `system_info()` executes\n\nWithin `system_info()`, there are 4 calls to `system_profiler SPHardwareDataType` (lines 42-44), each spawning a new process and taking 200-500ms. The total latency for this single command can exceed 2 seconds. These should be consolidated into a single call with cached output:\n\n```bash\nlocal hw_data\nhw_data=$(system_profiler SPHardwareDataType 2>/dev/null)\nmodel_name=$(echo \"$hw_data\" | grep 'Model Name' | ...)\nchip_info=$(echo \"$hw_data\" | grep 'Chip' | ...)\nmemory_info=$(echo \"$hw_data\" | grep 'Memory' | ...)\n```\n\n**The `set -euo pipefail` concern**: Multiple modules use pipe patterns like `ps aux | sort -nr -k 3 | head -10 | while read ...`. Under `pipefail`, if `head` closes the pipe early (which it does after reading 10 lines), the preceding `sort` gets SIGPIPE and exits non-zero. Under `set -e`, this should abort the script. The reason it currently works is that these pipelines run inside the `while read` loop's implicit subshell, and the exit code of the pipeline is not checked by the enclosing function. However, this is fragile and any change to the error handling strategy could cause breakage.\n\n**The screenshot_take() data flow bug**: `screenshot_take()` at `lib/screenshot.sh:400-433` saves screenshots to `/tmp/screenshot-$(date +%s).png` regardless of the configured screenshot location. After taking the screenshot, it prints \"Screenshot saved to: $location\" where `$location` is the configured location, not `/tmp`. The file is actually in `/tmp` but the user is told it is in the configured location. This is a clear data flow disconnect.\n\n## 6. Edge Case Handling (Score: 50/100)\n\n**Dangerous `/tmp/*` deletion**: `system_cleanup()` at `lib/system.sh:173` runs `rm -rf /tmp/*`. This is the most dangerous operation in the codebase. `/tmp` contains Unix sockets for running applications, PID files, temporary databases (SQLite WAL files for browsers), and named pipes. Deleting all of these can crash running applications or corrupt data. The `|| true` suppression hides any errors, giving the user false confidence. The fix is straightforward: use `find /tmp -type f -atime +7 -user $(whoami) -delete` to only clean old files owned by the current user.\n\n**Floating-point comparison inconsistency**: `dev_cpu_hogs()` uses string comparison for numeric thresholds (`[[ \"$cpu\" > 5.0 ]]`), while `dev_memory_hogs()` correctly uses `bc -l` for the same purpose. The string comparison fails for values >= 10 because lexicographic ordering puts \"10.0\" before \"5.0\" (since \"1\" < \"5\").\n\n**No IPv6 support**: `network_get_local_ip()` only returns IPv4 addresses via `ipconfig getifaddr`. On networks with IPv6-only connectivity, this returns nothing and the user is told \"No active network connection found\" despite having working IPv6 connectivity.\n\n**Battery parsing on desktop Macs**: `system_battery()` checks for SPPowerDataType availability but the check (`system_profiler SPPowerDataType >/dev/null 2>&1`) succeeds even on desktop Macs, returning data about AC power. The subsequent parsing of battery-specific fields (percentage, cycle count) may return empty strings, leading to incomplete output rather than a clear \"no battery\" message.\n\n**sudo commands without pre-check**: `network_flush_dns()` at `lib/network.sh:199-216` runs `sudo dscacheutil -flushcache` without checking if the user has sudo access. If the user does not have admin privileges, the command will prompt for a password in the middle of the operation, which is a poor user experience for a command that should check preconditions upfront.\n\n**The `find` command in `get_available_modules()`** at `lib/utils.sh:524-529` uses `find` to list modules. If the `lib/` directory ever contains non-module files (like `.DS_Store`, `__pycache__`, etc.), they would be listed as available modules. The `-name \"*.sh\" -not -name \"utils.sh\"` filter is good but could be stricter.\n\n**Memory page size hardcoding** as mentioned in the macOS API section causes all memory statistics to be wrong on Apple Silicon. This is the most impactful edge case since M-series Macs are now the majority of the installed base.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nSuperMac v2.1.0 demonstrates solid architectural design in its modular dispatcher pattern and consistent module interface. The routing system is well-structured with good error messages and global shortcuts. However, the implementation has several significant gaps:\n\n1. **Dead configuration system** (CRITICAL): config.json is never read at runtime. Users who edit it will see no effect.\n2. **Incorrect memory statistics on Apple Silicon** (HIGH): Hardcoded 4096-byte page size produces wrong numbers on the most common modern Macs.\n3. **Silently degraded WiFi functionality** (HIGH): The `airport` binary is never found because it is not on PATH, disabling advanced WiFi features without informing the user.\n4. **Destructive /tmp cleanup** (HIGH): `rm -rf /tmp/*` can break running applications.\n5. **12,800 lines of dead duplicate code** at the project root creates maintenance confusion.\n6. **No module re-sourcing guard** wastes resources during search and repeated invocations.\n\nThe codebase is well-intentioned and mostly functional for common use cases. The user-facing experience (color output, helpful tips, confirmation prompts) is polished. The core logic needs hardening around edge cases, macOS API correctness, and actually connecting the configuration system to the modules that should use it."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":22,"cache_creation_input_tokens":0,"cache_read_input_tokens":78592,"output_tokens":9249,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"type":"assistant","uuid":"1524873e-9f58-4eb2-ad4d-973538b88d4a","timestamp":"2026-04-07T13:23:14.698Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac","sessionId":"ee896f3b-ba3e-493e-ab51-73d0ef866e89","version":"2.1.92","gitBranch":"main","slug":"binary-sauteeing-dragonfly"}
